<userid>106589046417636429180</userid>< name>
Jiahui Zhou< /name>
<Date>1550269075035< /Date><rating>5<//rating>< Review>
What a wonderful lunch outdoor in the early spring. This is perhaps so far my favorite Asian-fusion restaurant in town. Plates were small and really meant to be shared. You cannot miss the lobster roll - golden airy ultra-crispy bread plus fresh lobster meat with minimalist seasoning - it must embody the soul of lobster rolls! The soup of the clam chowder was a bit too salty but the quality clams themselves were incomparable. We also loved the steak bao - the steak was so tender and juicy and there was such a refreshing harmony among all the ingredients. The dessert was named "cloudy with a chance of apples" - not only good-looking but truly tasty. Look forward to coming back later.<//Review>

< pics>
[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNq5v6wNJX5-WWQoqPm38TPQwz0_rWJ7e0fg6nB=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNEghFEmQJWzayRsOsnFhqHIH4xZLP3ViNKl89c=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOMTF03rsuLi9wDpKPrpQSGmYcxhle1Q-eHtfbu=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipO8fP_f4x05wnUPX65w-bnVLwKy4IpshfDL-uyA=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNw2CAkTzScM1b18pMyvnCGR2cMp2hgihiL-V02=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNhegCmtPelBTIBs_Vu9PaltEi2rC0kIoEY6gPk=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipML0B2pG31gRdSs5peBK6QnLT4r50kjqFo6zj_W=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPbmb_tO8eeZ2o5dz474nnJTNsBcJbd9DLcf43N=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOjrJas--J6Gt7WtarG63ja5CTNBr1iQbmCdXyO=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPsVbYZiUd4ZL8-Th6iVVWmvawRjcfaUg-3dQEf=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pics>
< Text>
Lukshon's "Heirloom Black Rice" is a twisted take on the spicy Indonesian fried rice dish, nasi goreng. Black rice, first harvested in China and thought to facilitate good health and long life, is not traditional in nasi goreng, and is often referred to as "forbidden rice" due to it being reserved exclusively for emperors during the Ching and Ming dynasties. On its own, it possesses a distinct nutty flavor and a firm, chewy texture. Here, it is stir-fried with sweet and smoky bits of lap cheong (Chinese sausage), onions, and so much roasted garlic I'm sure I still breathe out remnants of it today. On top of the rice rests a sunny-side up egg with whites set too loose for my liking. And although all of this stuff and a distinct blast of white pepper and diced chilis may seem overwhelming, it is the rice that is clearly the focus of the dish. I am unimpressed with my initial bite; it tastes familiar, but it's just garlicky fried rice, right? When half a bowl somehow disintegrates, I realize I have crossed the point of no return and I must finish the job. I pretend I'll treadmill it all off later.

I had similar reactions with all of the food I've eaten at Lukshon: despite relentless leverage of aromatics and pan-Asian flavor bombs, there is something evocative about it all, leaving the most compelling aspects of the dish understated, so that an impromptu craving is built for those shrouded elements. This appears to be the skilled and purposeful scheme of chef Sang Yoon, a French-trained cook of Korean origin, who worked for Wolfgang Puck and Joel Robuchon before revitalizing gastropub "Father's Office," where he's made his name selling one of L.A.'s best burgers: a medium-rare concoction on a garlic bun featuring a pungent blue cheese and a bacon compote.

The format here is much different: small plates of Asian comfort food given a "haute continental" treatment. Lukshon, a play on the Yiddish word for noodles (to honor Yoon's surrogate Jewish grandmother), is the kind of place that would have demanded crisp white linens and fine stemware before the post-gourmet revolution reduced our collective expectations for fine dining. This doesn't mean that Lukshon is frivolous. Quite the opposite: this is a serious restaurant operated by an autocrat who insists you eat by his rules.

What I admire most about Lukshon is the restaurant's intolerance for customers seeking to sabotage their meals. Don't bother asking for a substitution or omission, because Lukshon is not going to make you a peanut-free version of their dumplings, or vegetarian version of their black rice. There are plenty of other kitchens that will take your money and let you ruin your meal. When you make the kind of food that Yoon makes, there exists an artistic integrity to each dish, an amalgamation of personal beliefs, creativity, heart, and soul. I sympathize with those with allergies and insensitivities, but you can't expect serious creators to compromise their work for you. I'm red-green colorblind, but I'm not asking Warhol to dull the rich, vibrant hues of Marilyn Diptych so I can perceive them better.

My favorite dish here was the "Lobster Roll Banh Mi," two great sandwiches combined into one. On a buttered bun rests a rich, creamy lobster salad accessorized with a pig ear terrine flavored with soy sauce and rice wine with ginger and onions, similar to Filipino adobo. Then there are these funky pickles along with a shredded green papaya in a tangy and spicy nuoc cham vinaigrette (made with Yoon's house-made fish sauce), channeling a sum tum salad, but with cleaner, tidier flavors.

My server was knowledgeable about the menu and polite, but not yet worldly enough to discuss the dishes that inspired the menu. But worry not: Lukshon's subtle and spirited nods to southeast Asian classics offer a sumptuous primer beyond what a conversation with any server could ever deliver.< /Text>

<Text>You should give this place a try, especially if you have a modest size group (3-5) people so that everyone can share dishes.

The food is very good, the ambiance is great, service fantastic, drinks very good.

Food is broadly "Asian fusion" and draws from a number of influences. It's like an upscale pine and crane. You've got tea leaf salad, Dan Dan noodles, etc. Of course they have Brussels sprouts, which has replaced avocado toast as the overhyped dish of the moment.

Drinks are varied and tasty. Good scotch selection.

Service is fantastic: friendly, knowledgeable, accommodating, fast, unobtrusive.

Great design and layout. It's just a fun place to be.

Give it a try!< /Text>< pics>

<Rating>3< /Rating><text>Let me start by saying two things: 1) I've had szechuan pepper before  multiple times (the 'mouth-watering' kind) and 2) I've eaten at Michelin star restaurants around the world and shacks on the side of the road, which I consider equal if the food is up to snuff. Overall, I rate 5 stars as a perfect experience - 1 star for wait staff, 1 for ambiance, and 3 for food (presentation, taste/texture, and plating). I heard rave reviews of this restaurant and decided to treat my partner to dinner on our vacation. First, the wait staff were fine (1/2 point from me because when we walked in the couple in front of us were asking for a table, waving to the 'tasting tables' and the maitre d' [female] stated that they were for the 'tasting.' The customer did not understand and he asked again and got the same response. Visibly confused the customer accepted the 'no' and sat at the bar with his pair. An easy solution would be to say they were reserved but this was not done smoothly and for that it cost the review a half point). Second, and most importantly, we ordered the 'classics' course menu, each course is itemized for the review: (1) Butterfish - PHENOMENAL, we'll balanced with the bitter green shoots, this dish was well portioned and married flavors brilliantly; (2) Lobster 'Banh mi' - the lobster flavor was lost in the richness of the buttered brioche, also (and I might be picky because my partner is Vietnamese and I just got back from a Xmas dinner where they made fish sauce from scratch) the 'banh mi' was really nonexistent. I was left waiting for that deep flavor from the fish sauce that never came through or fermented veggies to cut the rich butter but that wasn't there either - overall this plate left me wanting; (3) Szechuan dumplings - I ate 1/2 of 1 and was completely turned off by the overpowering Szechuan pepper, it was not just 'there,' it was the ONLY flavor 'there.' In addition, after eating this small bite I began to feel nausea and a headache - this was the worst dish, for sure, and I would never order it again; (4) 'Beef and broccoli' - my biggest critique of this dish is the lack of seasoning. The beef and broccoli were well prepared and plated but the 'coating' [I don't know what else to call it because it wasn't a crust or a sauce] on the beef monopolized the taste of everything - the whole dish just tasted like that coating, which lacked salt, as well. I waited for another complementary flavor with the broccoli  like lemon or a bright element but the broccoli was just grilled, with no flavor at all to highlight the relationship between the crisp broccoli and the savory beef. This dish REQUIRED salt and with the coating taking over the dish I felt that it may do better as a small sauce on the plate or on the side - it was overall bland and moot; (5) soba noodles? - OVERPOWERING szechuan pepper again, infused deeply in the peanut sauce. I took a half of a bite and I almost threw up right then and there (side note: I actually threw up the whole dinner when we got back to the hotel :( 300 dollars down the drain) - enough said about that dish, it was, like the dumplings, monopolized by the pepper and was inedible, for me; (6) chocolate 'rocks' - PERFECT DISH, I wouldn't change anything about the dessert. With a perfect temper on the chocolate coating that married harmoniously with the ice cream inside and the cream sauce on the plate. This was complimented by the crunchy bits on the plate and an absolutely perfect passion fruit jelly, which brought all the flavors together so elegantly I couldn't stop eating this dish! Finally, the ambiance was great, but alas, I must give only 3 stars because of the comments above. Needless to say, my partner ended up paying for the dinner because he frlt bad that I didn't enjoy most of it, his critiques were not as itemized as mine but echoed some of the same as my own. In sum: Order al la carte if it's your first time - you also may want to taste the szechuan sauce before buying those items, you may not like it at all.</text>< Pictures>

< Text>
I seldom give a five stars, but Lukshon deserves that rating. The room is extraordinary, sleek, modern, comfortable and efficient. The staff is professional AND friendly. That alone is a rarity in upscale restaurants for some mysterious reason.

<text>When I first looked at the menu, I thought, why is this place $$$? These prices are normal! Then I ate there and understood why each person could easily spend $$$ for their fill.

Nevertheless, the food is delicious. I came here with my friend for DineLA week, and per the usual routine ordered off the DineLA menu and then some, but shared every single dish. It's just the right thing to do, despite what Joey says.

The watermelon salad with nuoc cham (a citrusy spicy sort of fish sauce - really wakes up the taste buds!) was really fresh. It made me appreciate how much better food is while in season - huge cubes of watermelon, microgreens, and the poached shrimp was a great addition.

Next came the spicy chicken pops - disappointing because they weren't spicy at all. Chicken was hot and tender though! I should also mention the soft shell crab here briefly - tempura fried perfectly with a really soft steamed bun, but nothing that was especially exciting. When we asked for a spicy sauce on the side, they gave us a blend of smoked chili peppers, but still more smoky than spicy.

The chiang mai curry noodles were definitely the star of the entrees, excluding dessert. I love curry noodle soup so this dish was a hit for me. Surprisingly spicy (questioning why the chicken pops weren't) and very savory, it was a great bowl of curry noodles for a one-man dinner!

Now for the real star of the dinner: the thai tea sundae. the scoop of thai tea flavored ice cream was so delicious, and everything that surrounded it was equally exciting. There were green citrus sauces, whipped coconut,  a caramel sauce with an interesting dark spice note to it. The whole dessert just came together like not other. If this were still offered on the regular menu, I would come back just for that.<//text><Pictures>None< /Pictures><Response>None</Response><gmapID>0x80c2b98253f81f7b:0x984bac857fbd77c7<//gmapID></record></dataset><record>

< Review>
This restaurant is billed as LA‚Äôs newest IT place. I showed up on on a sunny, pleasant early Saturday evening. The streets of Culver City were absurdly empty. I even found a *free* parking spot immediately.

We were seated at a communal table, weird because there were several empty tables in the seating area.

There are five seating areas: one outdoor, rest indoors: an area with booths, a ‚Äòcommunal‚Äô area with two large 8 seater tables, a row of 10 stools by the bar, and six stools that overlook the kitchen, for those who want to look at the proles that cook your food. Total capacity about 100 seats.

Service was efficient. The menus arrived quickly. No free bread. The waiter told us that it is typically 3 small plates person, which comes out to $30 per person. Many items on the menu looked good, and we ordered the Hawaiian Butterfish (15), Lobster Roll Banh Mi (17), Not Chinese Chicken Salad (13), Sichuan Dumplings (13), Brussels Sprouts (9), Spicy Chicken Pops (14), Crispy Rice Cakes (12), Heirloom Black Rice (13).

For drinks we ordered the Singapore Sling (14) and the Hot & Sour Gimlet (13). As a second act I ordered the black lager coedo ‚Äúshikkoku‚Äù dark beer (9)

For dessert we had the Warm Banana Toffee Cake(10), Warm Donuts (10) and the Coconut Dark Chocolate Rocks (11)

I am going to save you a lot of time and tell you what to do. You go here, order the Hawaiian Butterfish, the Heirloom Black Rice, the Coconut Dark Chocolate Rocks and the dark beer. Skip the rest.

The Hawaiian Butterfish is a salad. It looked amazing. As the first dish that came out, with a bit of the Gimlet in me, it looked so good. It tasted great. Great presentation. I had never eaten such firm fish flesh before, and was beguiled. What was this? I must find out.

Now, I had never heard of Butterfish before, and knew it was a marketing term. So I asked them what fish it was. They first came back with Escolar. I was like, come on. Escolar is a catch-all term for a group of fish. Exactly what fish is it? More conferring, they said it was ‚Äòwalu‚Äô.

A little Google work yielded some funny results. Walu is known as the ‚Äòpoop fish‚Äô or the ‚Äòex-lax fish‚Äô. Apparently the fish cannot digest fat and so its flesh is mostly fat. And if you eat more than 6 oz of it, you will experience some uncomfortable sensations as well. Go look it up.

But eat it! It tastes divine. Just. Not. Too. Much.

The Lobster Roll was so-so. The Not Chinese Chicken Salad was terrible. The Sichuan Dumplings, well let‚Äôs just say that they are not from Sichuan, the Sichuan sauce was meh, and they are more like micro-Dumplings. The Brussels Sprouts were OK, the 6 year old in our group ate all of them. The Crispy Rice Cakes were terrible.

The use of "Shelton Farms Drummettes‚Äù as a marketing term for selling the ‚ÄòSpicy Chicken Pops‚Äù is weird. Being in LA we don‚Äôt know of Shelton Farms, so in our money-addled status-grubby minds it conjures up visions of a bucolic farm where everything is organic, cows are milked by milkmaids, pigs speak prose and the chicken pecks away until the ax comes down. But Shelton Farms, as far as I could find in Google, is just some corner market in Michigan of all places. So did my chicken come frozen from 1,500 miles away?

There was nothing spicy about the Spicy Chicken Pops. Miniscule pieces of ‚Äòchicken‚Äô drowned in a sugary sauce.

The Heirloom Black Rice was delicious. I‚Äôd love to incorporate that into my regular eating schedule.

I saw a fried fish going out of the kitchen, a whole fried fish bent in half. Waiter said it was $45. What fish is it? He said branzino. Branzino? Deep fried? For $45? That‚Äôs insane. By my calculations, wholesale cost is $8.00 per lb, they are doing a 5x multiplier. Ripoff.

I was underwhelmed by this place. Other than two dishes, one dessert, and a beer, it was overpriced, overflavored food. The bill took my breath away.

So if you must go here, eat the Butterfish, the Heirloom Black Rice, drink the dark beer, eat the Rocks for dessert, and get out. Better yet, don't go.< /Review>

< Review>
Super chill atmosphere. Lots of space to sit or even lounge in couches. I can't speak on behalf of the food, but the drinks are absolutely incredible! They definitely have their own version of cocktails that I've never had before.

I was originally going to give four stars but on the last drink the bartender actually came over to our table and lit it on fire and did an entire show, it was so awesome! It was called the forbidden. He said he doesn't always do it tableside, so don't expect it, but when he has time he does.

We would recommend this. We will be back for happy hour.<//Review>

<Name>Velvet Overkil</Name><Date>1548295549331< /Date>< rate>
5<//rate>
< Review>
Darkly wood panelled place, dine in the pseudo "old" style. Overstuffed stools, a couch or two and a secondary bar level stooped area make for abundant seating. Service was uneven, as it took the staff over 10 minutes to notice that we were there (not many of them were out) but once we were noticed, a number of servers and associated workers appeared, as if they were all occupied elsewhere and just got let out; it was odd. The service, once the servers were "out", was prompt and professional. Drinks are not cheap but I had the feeling they are trying to represent themselves as an "established" place but the feel was more if an "upscaley" place; we're popular and you're fortunate to be eating our fine food. The food was quite good. The drinks were quite tasty (they know what they're doing) but I wouldn't go there for drinks (too little for what is charged) unless I pulled in 100k yearly, imho.  4.5 STARS< /Review>

<username>Grant ‚ÄúAlexander‚Äù Hammel-Davis<//username>< Date>
1595799057721< /Date>
< rate>
5</rate>
<text>White Horse is a really great place to visit for delicious New Orleans Cajun. The food and drinks are very well priced for the outstanding quality you get, and the servers and bartenders are extremely knowledgeable as well. Feel safe when visiting, everything is being done with the COVID best practice requirements. Great happy hour offerings as well, especially for those that like 'Old Fashioneds'. I really liked and appreciated the old school music and old fashioned dim bar surroundings, it really was refreshing. The dark wood and red upholstery The exterior design is very tasteful and catches your attention when passing by. The set up works great for those looking for a group setting or even just for couples. I found the brunch menu to be especially enticing, I'm going to need to come back a couple of times to try out all the things that looked promising. The parking structure is right next door for maximum convenience. This place is truly a hidden gem amongst all the other great places in Pasadena. I'm also looking forward to checking out their sister location, Craft Hill, which I've heard great things about. Brandon was an amazing team member and recommended the fried chicken sandwich, which was fantastic. He knew all the items on the menu almost from memory and went above and beyond to walk me through everything. I'm glad I went with his recommendations. He also told me some cool things to do in the area and South Pasadena, so I have those on my list as well. They don't skip on the portions either, you'll definitely satisfy your appetite and probably have some leftovers as well. I can't think of much they can do to improve things, everything was so great! I plan on visiting again sooner rather than later.</text>< Pictures>

I like to cook. I do. I really really do. So I already know when I go out to eat that I can prepare the meal I‚Äôm going to eat just as well as the restaurant for a fraction of the price. Therefore service, ambiance, and cleanliness are of the upmost importance to me.

<time>1583312770688<//time><Rating>2</Rating><review>A packed dining room and bar put this place quite in the limelight as you enter on a weekend evening. Unfortunately, there were far too many misses to honestly click on an extra star for the rating.

The bar seriously needs to pay attention to customers. Waiting for my party and waiting at the bar, and trying to get a drink was an impossible 5 minutes. They were treating me like I just came out of an AA meeting.

The menu seems to hit most of the notes for a hungry patron. At first glance, you can see it is well designed. Something for everyone wraps the context of each category. Fine Wagyu meats, a great burger, your standard salmon dish, and an attractive Southern Fried Chicken.

Dig deeper and you can find the pretentiousness of certain items. The use of Wagyu in smoked brisket, for example, is quite a redundancy. Why pay for a Wagyu priced cut that is supposed to be slow-smoked/cooked?

The Jumbalaya Rissoto is in fact not "risotto," and made with orzo pasta. Granted it is stated in the description as orzo, the title is completely misleading. If a person was gluten intolerant this would be a horrific experience. This dish is totally not worthy of the $26 price tag for a pasta dish.

The service felt like the servers were really working hard. I overheard a waiter mumbling about covering 8 large tables. I commend the service timing for everyone at the table.

The drinks here are very good. The bar certainly displays some craft behind their creations. I would return for their happy hour, and possibly a revisit for a sample of other items.

I do miss Cheval Blanc that once took this location to new heights in french cuisine.</review><pics>None< /pics>< response>

What a wonderful surprise!! The White Horse Lounge is a great place for family, out of town guest spot, romantic two or just friends! The food is an explosion of flavors and mouth watering treats! I kind you not.. the southern fried chicken is seasoned to delight, the Hoe cake made me moooan, the salmon avec haricot verts satisfies the palate with lightness.. and the drinks..well let's just say they don't hold back! Update:
We stopped by and has Arroyo hamburger which was fantastic. Big Josh, the chef stopped by and revealed that the every ingrediants used here is from a local and certified grower. We had Judy taken care of us.

Josh was proud of his cooking style learned from her Japanese granma.

A classy place with great selection and service. We just dropped in and got hooked.

We sat in and Cesar took our order. He suggested Strawberry Buck and Peach Schnapps to start with which were both sweet drinks and fit the occasion. Bertta, the manager stopped by and chatted with us over the specials for the night.

The Bread and Butter we got was warmly toasted with some  greens and slice of pork. We ordered Porklion and Arroyo Burger. Both were good and tasty. The portions were adequate.

We ended with Pear cobbler with scoop of ice cream. Well made and filling.<//review>
